<!-- Sticky Footer Ad --><div class="proper-ad-unit ad-sticky"><div id="proper-ad-ecowatch_sticky_1"><script> propertag.cmd.push(function() { proper_display('ecowatch_sticky_1'); }); </script></div></div><script>
 window.IcreateElementChangeListener= function (selector, callback) {
    const initializedNodes = new Set([]);

    document.querySelectorAll(selector).forEach((node) => {
        callback(node);
        initializedNodes.add(node);
    });

    const mutationObserver = new MutationObserver(() => {
        const nodes = document.querySelectorAll(selector);
        nodes.forEach((node) => {
            if (!initializedNodes.has(node)) {
                callback(node);
                initializedNodes.add(node);
            }
        });
    });

    mutationObserver.observe(document.body, {
        childList: true,
        subtree: true,
    });
}

 window.setCookie__ = function (cname,cvalue,exdays) {
    var d = new Date();
    d.setTime(d.getTime() + (exdays * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000));
    var expires = "expires="+d.toUTCString();
   
    document.cookie = cname + "=" + cvalue + ";" + expires +";path=/"; ;
}

window.getCookie= function (cname) {
    var name = cname + "=";
    var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
    var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
    for(var i = 0; i < ca.length; i++) {
        var c = ca[i];
        while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
            c = c.substring(1);
        }
        if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
            return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
        }
    }
    return "";
}

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>By <span style="background-color: initial;">Andrea Germanos</span></p><p><span style="background-color: initial;"></span>A recent series of summer droughts in Europe, which brought <a href="https://www.dw.com/en/deadly-fires-rage-in-portugal-spain-ex-hurricane-ophelia-fans-flames/a-40968565" target="_blank">devastating</a> <a href="https://www.newsweek.com/massive-drought-leaves-over-one-million-dead-fish-carcasses-reeking-and-1289906" target="_blank">ecological</a>, <a href="https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-barley-brewing-idUSKCN1NE1BW" target="_blank">agricultural</a>, and economic impacts, were more severe than any over the past 2,100 years, new research out Monday <a href="https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210315-europe-s-droughts-since-2015-worst-in-2-000-years" target="_blank">finds</a>.</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
                    &lt;p&gt;"Our results show that what we have experienced over the past five summers is extraordinary for central Europe, in terms of how dry it has been consecutively," dendrochronology specialist and lead author Professor Ulf Bntgen of Cambridge's Department of Geography &lt;a href="https://www.cam.ac.uk/stories/europeandrought" target="_blank"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; in a statement.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Bntgen and the team of international researchers linked the recent droughts to the climate crisis, including its impacts on the jet stream.&lt;/p&gt;
                    
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/europe-drought-crisis" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651103839" data-published-at="1615920372" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;div id="45d91" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="f2ee65d71819aa86d8c43c6e0aa667fc"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1371511771702378496" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;The chemical fingerprints in European oak trees show that in 2015, #drought conditions in Europe suddenly intensifi https://t.co/hdOGC6CZD2&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; Cambridge University (@Cambridge University)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/Cambridge_Uni/statuses/1371511771702378496"&gt;1615828862.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The findings were &lt;a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/s41561-021-00698-0" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;published&lt;/a&gt; Monday in the journal &lt;em&gt;Nature Geoscience&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Analyzing more than 27,000 measurements of carbon and oxygen isotopic ratios from European oak trees  21 living and 126 dead  the scientists got a picture of past climates, including summer droughts, spanning the years 75 BC to 2018.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Co-author Paolo Cherubini of the Federal Research Institute WSL in Birmensdorf, Switzerland, explained that "carbon values depend on the photosynthetic activity" and "oxygen values are affected by the source water."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And the "insights before medieval times," said Bntgen, "are particularly vital, because they enable us to get a more complete picture of past drought variations, which were essential for the functioning and productivity of ecosystems and societies."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The reconstruction showed an overall drying trend. But the samples showed that the droughts from 2015-2018 were "unprecedented" over the massive time span.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But the runaway climate crisis portends more worrisome parched periods to come.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Climate change does not mean that it will get drier everywhere: some places may get wetter or colder, but extreme conditions will become more frequent, which could be devastating for agriculture, ecosystems, and societies as a whole," said Bntgen.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The U.K. Green Party shared &lt;em&gt;The Guardian&lt;/em&gt;'s reporting on the new study with a &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/TheGreenParty/status/1371826010006650886" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;tweet&lt;/a&gt; declaring, "Climate change is here."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"If we don't cut carbon emissions, it will get worse," they said. "Let's fight this while it's still fixable."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

                    &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://www.commondreams.org/news/2021/03/16/climate-change-here-europes-recent-droughts-unprecedented-millennia-study-finds" target="_blank"&gt;Common Dreams&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<div class="around-the-web"><div class="from-your-site__headline">From Your Site Articles</div>

        Hawaii Moves to Ban More Reef-Harming Sunscreens

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>Hawaii is on its way to banning more reef-damaging <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/sunscreen" target="_self">sunscreens</a>. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/hawaii-sunscreen-ban" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101992" data-published-at="1615914985" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;On Tuesday of last week, its state Senate approved &lt;a href="https://www.capitol.hawaii.gov/measure_indiv.aspx?billtype=SB&amp;amp;billnumber=132&amp;amp;year=2021" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Senate Bill 132&lt;/a&gt;, which would ban all sunscreens containing the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/chemicals" target="_self"&gt;chemicals&lt;/a&gt; avobenzone or octocrylene. The bill then moved to the House, where it passed its first reading on Thursday, March 11. If approved, it would build on a &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/hawaii-coral-reefs-sunscreen-ban-2565189657.html" target="_self"&gt;2018 law&lt;/a&gt; that banned sunscreens containing the chemicals oxybenzone and octinoxate, which went into effect this January.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/hawaii-sunscreen-ban" data-id="2" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101992" data-published-at="1615914985" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMzkxOS9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYzOTQ3Nzg4MH0.E-MK-chqqslmq6jbBsEVqoqeUcEu3nhvsMXrQWIb7zk/img.png?width=980" id="9bb37" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="6d12a10f80f25370cf31dc4433f42a21" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1250" data-height="702" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>Coastal Oahu, Hawaii and the Kualoa Ranch. Hawaii is considering banning more reef-harming sunscreens to protect its unique coral reefs. <em>Art Wager / E+ / Getty Images</em></p></small>&lt;p&gt;"This is great news for our imperiled &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/coral-reefs" target="_self"&gt;coral reefs&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/marine-life" target="_self"&gt;marine life&lt;/a&gt;," Maxx Phillips, Hawai'i director and staff attorney at the Center for Biological Diversity (CBD), &lt;a href="https://biologicaldiversity.org/w/news/press-releases/hawaii-senate-bill-bans-harmful-sunscreen-chemicals-2021-03-09/" target="_blank"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; in response to the Senate vote. "People can protect their skin without harmful petrochemicals while Hawai'i protects public and environmental health."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The bill comes amidst growing scientific awareness of the impact of common sunscreen chemicals on marine life. These chemicals can make corals more susceptible to viral infections and &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/coral-bleaching" target="_self"&gt;bleaching&lt;/a&gt;, as well as disrupting the reproductive systems of &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/fish" target="_self"&gt;fish&lt;/a&gt; and other animals, the &lt;a href="https://www.staradvertiser.com/2021/03/12/breaking-news/sunscreen-bill-banning-more-reef-unfriendly-chemicals-in-hawaii-advances-legislature/" target="_blank"&gt;Honolulu Star Advertiser reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/hawaii-sunscreen-ban" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101992" data-published-at="1615914985" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;In particular, octocrylene can disrupt human hormones and harm marine animals, according to the CBD. A soon-to-be-published study has found it can break down into the carcinogenic benzophenone, which also kills plants and disrupts reproduction. Avobenzone, meanwhile, is also an endocrine disruptor and can make coral less resilient to the high temperatures caused by the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/" target="_self"&gt;climate crisis&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Studies show fish exposed to octocrylene exhibited endocrine disruption, brain deformities in larvae and reproductive toxicity," ecotoxicologist Craig Downs told the CBD. "Because octocrylene bioaccumulates, what does that mean for people eating these fish, especially pregnant women and keiki? Avobenzone may cause a dysfunction with the powerhouse of the cell, which may kill cells and induce a bleaching effect in corals."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/hawaii-sunscreen-ban" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101992" data-published-at="1615914985" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;The CBD has petitioned the Food and Drug Administration (FDA) to ban these chemicals on the national level, but for now it falls to Hawaii to protect its unique ecosystems: Around one fourth of all of the plants, fish and invertebrates found on Hawaii's reefs are native to the archipelago.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If it passes, the bill would go into effect Jan. 1, 2023. It will ban the sale or distribution of any sunscreen containing the targeted chemicals unless the buyer has a valid prescription. For those looking to protect themselves from the sun without harming ocean life, scientists and the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA) recommend products containing non-nanoized titanium dioxide and non-nanoized zinc oxide, the Honolulu Star Advertiser reported.&lt;/p&gt;</div>

        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>In this guide, we break down the best and most popular <a data-linked-post="2649648885" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/essential-oils-for-anxiety-2649648885.html" target="_blank">essential oils</a> on the market today. Keep reading to discover the many different types of essential oils, their uses, and incredible benefits.<br/></p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
                    &lt;h2&gt;What are essential oils?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/lifestyle/wellness/essential-oils-are-potent-risky-and-promising-heres-what-you-need-to-know/2019/12/10/1470d7c4-1623-11ea-8406-df3c54b3253e_story.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Essential oils&lt;/a&gt; are potent, highly concentrated extracts from plants. Many of them have been used for centuries with the primary objective of promoting wellness and wellbeing. Aside from that, they are also an excellent way to connect with an ancient and profound part of nature.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Essential oils provide a natural alternative to chemical products made with synthetic components, which can often be unsafe or untrustworthy. For many people, this makes &lt;a data-linked-post="2649941651" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/detox-and-boost-your-immunity-2649941651.html" target="_blank"&gt;plant therapy&lt;/a&gt; a better option for body care, or home use. Common uses of essential oils include aromatherapy, taking care of your skin, easing muscle pain, or merely cleaning and perfuming your home. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;The best essential oils&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;You may not know it yet, but essential oils can be used to enhance many day-to-day activities. You can find countless synergistic practices for the best essential oils to use in your daily routine. Let's take a look at our favorite essential oils and what makes them so great.&lt;/p&gt;
                    
<div class="rebellt-item rebellt-ecommerce is--desktop col1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/best-essential-oils" data-id="1" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651052021" data-published-at="1615655218" id="rebelltitem1"><h3 data-role="headline"><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Cliganic-Peppermint-Essential-Therapeutic-Aromatherapy/dp/B07QB8DL5N/ref=sr_1_7?dchild=1&amp;keywords=peppermint%2Bessential%2Boil&amp;qid=1615477524&amp;s=hpc&amp;sr=1-7&amp;th=1" target="_blank">Peppermint</a></h3>&lt;img type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgyMTE1My9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2NTExMzc4NX0.Gl4mwHp6hi7-g4gBOoFK8ey6cao9Izr8tZz4tekhE84/img.png?width=980" id="cbde2" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="fddead1d3c364bcf8a0ad9e1a081785e" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image" alt="Peppermint essential oil"  data-width="400" data-height="400" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>cliganic.com</p></small>&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.amazon.com/Cliganic-Peppermint-Essential-Therapeutic-Aromatherapy/dp/B07QB8DL5N/ref=sr_1_7?dchild=1&amp;amp;keywords=peppermint%2Bessential%2Boil&amp;amp;qid=1615477524&amp;amp;s=hpc&amp;amp;sr=1-7&amp;amp;th=1" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Peppermint essential oil&lt;/a&gt; is extracted from the plant before it actually blooms, which is why it is much more concentrated than other essential oils. Its main ingredient is menthol and is trendy in cosmetics since it brings significant benefits to the skin, hair, and of course, your general well-being.&lt;/p&gt;

    <div class="rebellt-ecommerce--sum">
<div class="rebellt-ecommerce--price">

</div>

                    &lt;h2&gt;What to look for in the best essential oils&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Getting started in the world of essential oils can be overwhelming due to the amount of information, uses, interpretations, and varieties that are available. That is why having concise information on what to look for in your oils will always result in a better experience. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Three factors you should always consider when looking for essential oils are the quality, the price, and the bottle.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Quality&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;The best aromatherapy oils must be 100% pure and organic with a scent that properly corresponds to the part of the plant from which it was extracted. If that is not the case, you may have reason to suspect that the oil is a sham that contains additives or fillers. One important factor in quality is the extraction method. Look for products that are USDA-certified organic whenever possible to be sure that the plants and flowers used are free from pesticides.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The extraction method is the process used in order to achieve the separation of aromatic compounds from the physical plant. These processes largely determine the quality standard of the final product. Find an oil extracted by the following organic methods to guarantee that toxic solvents sometimes used for such separation are not in your essential oil.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The first is cold-pressed extraction. This is the more popular option for essential citrus oils, and works by exposing the skin of the fruit or pericarp to mechanical pressure. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Steam distillation, which works by subjecting bits of plant matter to a stream of water vapor, is the other preferred extraction method. The essence is condensed in this process and then collected by separating it from the water. While there are other methods to distill essential oils, these are the best to guarantee quality.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Pricing&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Next up is the question of pricing. While we can be wary of the "higher price, higher quality" theory in some products, you shouldn't look to skimp on essential oils. Prices can also vary widely between different types of oils. It is rare to walk into a shop and find all of the essential oil extractions are priced the same. If the oils are truly 100% natural, they shouldn't share the same price since not all plants are equally as accessible.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Costs can vary depending on the raw material used, transportation costs, and special storage requirements, making the final value vary a lot. For example, the number of roses required to extract an ounce of oil is quite high, unlike lavender which is much more accessible. This is why the price of these two oils will be very different if it is a 100% original extraction. You can find many popular essential oil brands like doTerra, Plant Therapy, Aura Cacia, and Vitruvi on Amazon that offer pure essential oils. Always be sure to check for the signs of quality when purchasing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Bottle&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finally, the essential oil bottle should always be made of glass and carry a dark tint. Look for a blue, amber, or dark brown tonality. This is crucial because most essential oils are very volatile and &lt;a href="https://www.tutallernatural.com/blog/la-calidad-y-conservacion-de-los-aceites-esenciales/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;evaporate quickly&lt;/a&gt; in contact with the light. Remember, plastic is the bigger enemy here. If quality matters to you, essential oils should be bottled and stored with the same care as you would expect with an expensive bottle of wine. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;How does aromatherapy work?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;A Persian doctor, Avicenna, wrote extensively on health and wellness and is known as the father of &lt;a href="https://ifaroma.org/en_GB/home/explore_aromatherapy/about-aromatherapy" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;aromatherapy&lt;/a&gt;. Still, it was actually Ren-Maurice Gattefosse (chemist and perfumer) who coined the term. This &lt;a href="https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2221169115001033" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;ancient practice&lt;/a&gt; is widely used around the world because its effects are rapid and widely recognized. For many people, tapping into the power of the mind, and calming the soul, is seen as a more desirable solution to their ailments than daunting prescriptions. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;One interesting explanation for why aromatherapy may work for many people is that the part of the brain that associates odors is the same part of the brain that deals with memory. Stimulating this part of the brain generates a response in the body naturally. The smell is undoubtedly one of the most primitive senses since it allows messages to be sent through the nervous system to the limbic system, the part of the brain that controls emotions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;What are the benefits of essential oils?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Inhaling or applying &lt;a href="https://pdfs.semanticscholar.org/88e3/78a02698d6bfd3850126c7c0733ce4763769.pdf" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;essential oils&lt;/a&gt; activates the hypothalamus, which is the brain area in charge of sending messages to other parts of the body. Benefits mentioned by consumers include promoting sensations of clear breathing, providing digestive well-being, boosting the immune system, creating a relaxing environment for rest, as well as contributing to a multitude of skin, hair, and teeth benefits. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Even though they are very rare, the few adverse side effects reported are mucous, skin, and eye irritations. Most of the cases recorded are due to inadequate storage conditions. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;What is the best way to use essential oils?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;There are two main ways to best access the &lt;a href="https://naha.org/explore-aromatherapy/about-aromatherapy/methods-of-application/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;benefits of essential oils&lt;/a&gt;: aromatic application and topical application.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Aromatic application&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;The first option involves the smelling or inhalation of your essential oil's aroma through direct inhalation, diffusion, or evaporation. The last two are typically done through diffusers, humidifiers, or using essential oil burners. Essential oil diffusers are an easy and generally inexpensive way to enjoy your essential oil through a device that disperses essential oils into the air through evaporation, or steam. Ease of use, stream intensity, water capacity, and appearance are items to look for when buying one.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Using a diffuser is as simple as choosing the place where you will enjoy your aromatherapy session. It is important to be aware of any allergies or medical conditions of other people who may be around, and if there are children, pets, or pregnant women. Then fill the water tank of the diffuser with clean water at room temperature and add a few drops of the oil. The regular capacity of diffusers is 100ml and it is advisable to use 4 to 6 drops of your essential oil. This quantity varies depending on the taste of the person, the size of the room as well as its temperature.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Topical application&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Applying essential oils on the skin, or topical application, is another way to use them. But for this method, it is important to know which dilutions and carrier oils to use, so you don't accidentally irritate the skin. The most common way to massage the oil onto the body is with a lotion, cream, roll-on, or carrier oil like coconut oil. This way the aromatic molecules are able to penetrate the skin. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In body massages the oil can be rubbed on pressure points such as your temples, wrists, forehead, or even feet. Again, being mindful of the dilution rate is key. Fifteen drops per one ounce of base oil are the standard for an adult, giving a 2.5% dilution rate. Warm compresses on the forehead and neck with a few drops are also recommended or applying approximately 2 -12 drops of essential oil to a bath, including the dispersing agent. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And remember, any questions or concerns you have about the composition, use, or effects of the oils as a treatment for any condition or simply their use for fun should be consulted with a certified doctor.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Discover the benefits of the best essential oils&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our ancestors used the natural world to take care of themselves and their families. As long as they're created in an environmentally sustainable fashion, essential oils and essential oil blends can continue to serve us today by promoting mental, physical, and spiritual well-being.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Sarita Vanegas&lt;/strong&gt; is a writer based in Medelln, Columbia, where she covers environmentally-friendly products, natural health, and plant-based remedies. A former Baselang teacher, she is also passionate about learning languages and exploring other cultures.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<div class="around-the-web"><div class="from-your-site__headline">From Your Site Articles</div>

<h2 class="widget__headline h2">
<a aria-label="Ancient Leaves Preserved Under Greenlands Ice Reveal Climate Secrets" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history-2651101362.html">
        Ancient Leaves Preserved Under Greenlands Ice Reveal Climate Secrets
    </a>
</h2>
<div class="social-author clearfix">
<div class="social-author__avatar image">
<div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy82NzI1NTU3L29yaWdpbi5qcGciLCJleHBpcmVzX2F0IjoxNjQ3NTIxOTEwfQ.RRiCDsOja8F3DatceLE6FbT3uo6F9-1QV9_s0V8Hr34/img.jpg?width=210")'></div>

<a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/science/">Science</a>

"\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, {"amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>
	By Andrew Christ and Paul Bierman
</p><p>
	In 1963, inside a covert U.S. military base in northern Greenland, a team of scientists <a href="https://icedrill.org/sites/default/files/SR-126.pdf" target="_blank">began drilling</a> down through the Greenland ice sheet. Piece by piece, they extracted an ice core 4 inches across and nearly a mile long. At the very end, they pulled up something else  12 feet of frozen soil.
</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
                    &lt;p&gt;
	&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
                    
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;The ice told a story of Earth's climate history. The frozen soil was examined, set aside and then forgotten.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Half a century later, scientists rediscovered that soil in a Danish freezer. It is now revealing its secrets.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Using lab techniques unimaginable in the 1960s when the core was drilled, we and an international team of fellow scientists were able to show that Greenland's massive ice sheet had melted to the ground there within the past million years. Radiocarbon dating shows that it would have happened more than 50,000 years ago. It most likely happened during times when the climate was warm and sea level was high, possibly 400,000 years ago.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And there was more. As we explored the soil under a microscope, we were stunned to discover the remnants of a tundra ecosystem  twigs, leaves and moss. We were looking at northern Greenland as it existed the last time the region was ice-free. Our &lt;a href="https://doi.org/10.1073/pnas.2021442118" target="_blank"&gt;peer-reviewed study&lt;/a&gt; was published on March 15 in &lt;a href="https://www.pnas.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="2" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjM5NS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2OTExNzg1NH0.MciQn_ezzYLK219Zln4KGBujp--kfXXY36U0cUFFZUA/img.jpg?width=980" id="ba2f8" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="bf45aa7cf7baa5060f98103d98f60efe" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="1584" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p><span style="background-color: initial;">Engineers pull up a section of the 4,560-foot-long ice core at Camp Century in the 1960s.</span> <span style="background-color: initial;"><a href="https://usace.contentdm.oclc.org/digital/collection/p15141coll5/id/654/" target="_blank"><em>U.S. Army Corps of Engineers</em></a></span></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;span style="display:block;position:relative;padding-top:56.25%;" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="d96b5bddbca32777f1566525e4803371"&gt;&lt;iframe lazy-loadable="true" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/Ota2-eEN41w?rel=0" width="100%" height="auto"  frameborder="0" scrolling="no" style="position:absolute;top:0;left:0;width:100%;height:100%;"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;/span&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;With no ice sheet, sunlight would have warmed the soil enough for tundra vegetation to cover the landscape. The oceans around the globe would have been more than 10 feet higher, and &lt;a href="https://scied.ucar.edu/learning-zone/climate-change-impacts/greenlands-ice-melting" target="_blank"&gt;maybe even 20 feet&lt;/a&gt;. The land on which Boston, London and Shanghai sit today would have been under the ocean waves.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;All of this happened before humans began warming Earth's climate. &lt;a href="https://climate.nasa.gov/climate_resources/24/graphic-the-relentless-rise-of-carbon-dioxide/" target="_blank"&gt;The atmosphere at that time contained far less carbon dioxide&lt;/a&gt; than it does today, and it wasn't rising as quickly. The ice core and the soil below are something of a Rosetta Stone for understanding how durable the Greenland ice sheet has been during past warm periods  and how quickly it might melt again as the climate heats up.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;h3&gt;Secret Military Bases and Danish Freezers&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;The story of the ice core begins during the Cold War with a military mission dubbed Project Iceworm. Starting around 1959, the U.S. Army hauled hundreds of soldiers, heavy equipment and even a nuclear reactor across the ice sheet in northwest Greenland and dug a base of tunnels inside the ice. They called it &lt;a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1Ujx_pND9wg" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Camp Century&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;It was part of a secret plan to hide nuclear weapons from the Soviets. The public knew it as an Arctic research laboratory. Walter Cronkite even paid a visit and &lt;a href="https://www.historicfilms.com/tapes/2705" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;filed a report&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="6" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem6">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjQwNi9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYxNzA5OTg0Nn0.cbuCsR7Rf-RsjkK-39JbZ9eTVgiwf5JFr4bUwO5-ozU/img.jpg?width=980" id="f49a8" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="f3dc831dab5e86116ad7f2d57fca2f2f" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="970" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p><span style="background-color: initial;">Workers build the snow tunnels at the Camp Century research base in 1960.</span> <span style="background-color: initial;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Century#/media/File:Camp_Century_trench_construction.png" target="_blank"><em>U.S. Army Corps of Engineers</em></a></span></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-7" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem7">&lt;p&gt;Camp Century didn't last long. The snow and ice began slowly crushing the buildings inside the tunnels below, forcing the military to abandon it in 1966. During its short life, however, scientists were able to extract the ice core and begin analyzing Greenland's climate history. &lt;a href="https://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/news/picture-climate-what-can-we-learn-ice" target="_blank"&gt;As ice builds up&lt;/a&gt; year by year, it captures layers of volcanic ash and changes in precipitation over time, and it traps air bubbles that reveal the past composition of the atmosphere.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;One of the original scientists, glaciologist Chester Langway, kept the core and soil samples frozen at the University at Buffalo for years, then he shipped them to a Danish archive in the 1990s, where the soil was soon forgotten.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A few years ago, our Danish colleagues found the soil samples in a box of glass cookie jars with faded labels: "Camp Century Sub-Ice."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-8" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="8" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem8">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjQxMi9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYxOTU3MjY2OH0.aB_UUQpd3PjIQ3-k76mhn0JrowP7KVOA-LB_rVfm_HQ/img.jpg?width=980" id="2c672" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="33cf0c063de7e9a03547e81c9a126673" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="900" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p><span style="background-color: initial;">Geomorphologist Paul Bierman (right) and geochemist Joerg Schaefer of Columbia University examine the jars holding Camp Century sediment for the first time. They were in a Danish freezer set at -17 F.</span> <span style="background-color: initial;"><em>Paul Bierman / </em><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nd/4.0/" target="_blank"><em>CC BY-ND</em></a></span></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-9" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="9" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem9">&lt;h3&gt;A Surprise Under the Microscope&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;On a hot July day in 2019, two samples of soil arrived at our &lt;a href="https://www.uvm.edu/cosmolab/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;lab at the University of Vermont&lt;/a&gt; frozen solid. We began the painstaking process of splitting the precious few ounces of frozen mud and sand for different analyses.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, we photographed the layering in the soil before it was lost forever. Then we chiseled off small bits to examine under the microscope. We melted the rest and saved the ancient water.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Then came the biggest surprise. While we were washing the soil, we spotted something floating in the rinse water. &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=nZ6d2zUAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Paul&lt;/a&gt; grabbed a pipette and some filter paper, &lt;a href="https://scholar.google.com/citations?user=FlafCtYAAAAJ&amp;amp;hl=en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Drew&lt;/a&gt; grabbed tweezers and turned on the microscope. We were absolutely stunned as we looked down the eyepiece.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Staring back at us were leaves, twigs and mosses. This wasn't just soil. This was an ancient ecosystem perfectly preserved in Greenland's natural deep freeze.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-10" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="10" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem10">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjQyOS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyMjQ1OTAwNH0.8U7PJm0S2CNARTputHp4kGarDuJ2FOXnBGWEtnwqlAM/img.jpg?width=980" id="d3969" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="c33b832095c6e6aacd5ab1cfc37d0154" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="900" /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-11" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="11" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem11">&lt;h3&gt;Dating Million-Year-Old Moss&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;How old were these plants?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over the last million years, Earth's climate was punctuated by relatively short warm periods, typically lasting about 10,000 years, called interglacials, when there was less ice at the poles and sea level was higher. The Greenland ice sheet survived through all of human history during the Holocene, the present interglacial period of the last 12,000 years, and most of the interglacials in the last million years.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But our research shows that at least one of these interglacial periods was warm enough for a long enough period of time to melt large portions of the Greenland ice sheet, allowing a tundra ecosystem to emerge in northwestern Greenland.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We used two techniques to determine the age of the soil and the plants. First, we used &lt;a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCSb1dSMVGCr4PzdooW5qSOQ" target="_blank"&gt;clean room chemistry&lt;/a&gt; and a &lt;a href="https://www.physics.purdue.edu/primelab/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;particle accelerator&lt;/a&gt; to count atoms that form in rocks and sediment when exposed to natural radiation that bombards Earth. Then, a colleague used an ultra-sensitive method for measuring &lt;a href="http://www.usu.edu/geo/luminlab/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;light emitted from grains of sand&lt;/a&gt; to determine the last time they were exposed to sunlight.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-12" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="12" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem12">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjQ0OC9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYzNzA2NTE0M30.B4NJm-S8l22ekdSnfNU448JKW-uDQa47m6ImQVEnQ34/img.png?width=980" id="019c3" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="324d149bbb8737180be078cbccbcd4b8" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="996" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p><span style="background-color: initial;">Maps of Greenland show the speed of the ice sheet as it flows (left) and the landscape hidden beneath it (right).</span> <span style="background-color: initial;"><em>BedMachine v3; Copernicus Climate Change Service (C3S) / </em><em><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nd/4.0/" target="_blank">CC BY-ND</a></em></span></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-13" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="13" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem13">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjQ1Ni9vcmlnaW4uZ2lmIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyNDc1MDk4NH0.sz1tK1JrD10GcvXJOTWZAKKwhgyVj0IPUajOJhRR--Q/img.gif?width=980" id="81208" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="e2515512b21c689e2a2927291e0cc14a" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="798" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>The concentration of carbon dioxide in the atmosphere today is well beyond past levels determined from ice cores. On March 14, 2021, the CO2 level was about 417 ppm.<em> </em><em><a href="https://climate.nasa.gov/vital-signs/carbon-dioxide/" target="_blank">NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a> / </em><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nd/4.0/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"><em>CC BY-ND</em></a></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-14" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="14" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem14">&lt;p&gt;The million-year time frame is important. &lt;a href="https://doi.org/10.1038/nature20146" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Previous work on another ice core, GISP2, extracted from central Greenland&lt;/a&gt; in the 1990s, showed that the ice had also been absent there within the last million years, perhaps about 400,000 years ago.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-15" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="15" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem15">&lt;p&gt;Losing the Greenland ice sheet would be catastrophic to humanity today. The melted ice would raise sea level by more than 20 feet. That would redraw coastlines worldwide.&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;About 40% of the global population &lt;a href="https://www.un.org/sustainabledevelopment/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/Ocean-fact-sheet-package.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;lives within 60 miles of a coast&lt;/a&gt;, and 600 million people live within 30 feet of sea level. &lt;a href="https://nca2018.globalchange.gov/chapter/9/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;If warming continues&lt;/a&gt;, ice melt from Greenland and Antarctica will pour more water into the oceans. Communities will be forced to relocate, climate refugees will become more common, and costly infrastructure will be abandoned. Already, &lt;a href="https://www.ipcc.ch/srocc/home/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;sea level rise has amplified&lt;/a&gt; flooding from coastal storms, causing hundreds of billions of dollars of damage every year.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-16" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="16" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem16">&lt;img lazy-loadable="true" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTgzMjQ2MC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY1MTgzNjUzOX0.cnfpFmjes7Z54c-XH4dxSMtR8CbNCMK4GhbKaJO8o44/img.jpg?width=980" id="8c511" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="2300ab4a9407a78d5a15ea12844cc25d" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   data-width="1200" data-height="1252" /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>Tundra near the Greenland ice sheet today. Is this what Camp Century looked like before the ice came back sometime in the last million years? <em>Paul Bierman / </em><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nd/4.0/" target="_blank"><em>CC BY-ND</em></a></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-17" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/greenland-ice-ecosystem-history" data-id="17" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101362" data-published-at="1615913780" id="rebelltitem17">&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href="https://www.sciencemag.org/news/2019/10/ancient-soil-secret-greenland-base-suggests-earth-could-lose-lot-ice" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;story of Camp Century&lt;/a&gt; spans two critical moments in modern history. An Arctic military base built in response to the existential threat of nuclear war inadvertently led us to discover another threat from ice cores  the threat of sea level rise from human-caused climate change. Now, its legacy is helping scientists understand how Earth responds to a changing climate.&lt;/p&gt;</div>

                    &lt;p&gt;
	&lt;em&gt;Andrew Christ is a postdoctoral fellow and lecturer in geology at the University of Vermont.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;
	 &lt;em&gt;Paul Bierman is a fellow of the Gund Institute for Environment and professor of geology and natural resources at the University of Vermont.&lt;/em&gt;

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>The <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/montreal-protocol" target="_self">Montreal Protocol</a> banning <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/ozone" target="_self">ozone</a>-depleting <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/chlorofluorocarbons" target="_self">chlorofluorocarbons</a> (CFCs) in 1987 has been <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/ozone-recovery-2522813339.html" target="_self">hailed</a> as an example of successful international collaboration to stop an environmental threat. But, like a creature from a horror movie, those banned <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/chemicals" target="_self">chemicals</a> could rise from the depths to stalk our atmosphere once again. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/cfc-ozone-ocean" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100772" data-published-at="1615912922" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;That's the finding of a new study, which concluded that the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/oceans" target="_self"&gt;ocean&lt;/a&gt; would shift from absorbing to releasing at least one type of CFC, known as CFC-11, by the end of this century. By the mid-2100s, the ocean could emit enough to be detectable.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"By the time you get to the first half of the 22nd century, you'll have enough of a flux coming out of the ocean that it might look like someone is cheating on the Montreal Protocol, but instead, it could just be what's coming out of the ocean," Susan Solomon, study co-author and Lee and Geraldine Martin Professor of Environmental Studies in MIT's Department of Earth, Atmospheric and Planetary Sciences, said in an &lt;a href="https://news.mit.edu/2021/oceans-emitting-cfc-ozone-0315" target="_blank"&gt;MIT press release.&lt;/a&gt; "It's an interesting prediction and hopefully will help future researchers avoid getting confused about what's going on."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The research, led by MIT, is newly published in the &lt;a href="https://www.pnas.org/content/118/12/e2021528118" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences&lt;/a&gt;. To draw their conclusions, researchers used models to simulate the ocean's current and future uptake and release of CFC-11. They found that by 2075, the ocean would emit more of the chemical than it absorbed. By 2145, it would release enough to be detectable by existing technologies.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/cfc-ozone-ocean" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100772" data-published-at="1615912922" id="rebelltitem2"><h3 data-role="headline"></h3>&lt;span style="display:block;position:relative;padding-top:56.25%;" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="f61acc856f6d0ee06221f3a64d7a2451"&gt;&lt;iframe lazy-loadable="true" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/SWNKHo-aiKU?rel=0" width="100%" height="auto"  frameborder="0" scrolling="no" style="position:absolute;top:0;left:0;width:100%;height:100%;"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;/span&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/cfc-ozone-ocean" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100772" data-published-at="1615912922" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;The models found that this process could be sped up by the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/" target="_self"&gt;climate crisis&lt;/a&gt;. If the planet warms by five degrees Celsius by 2100, the ocean will become a net emitter of CFC-11 by 2065 and release detectable levels by 2140.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Generally, a colder ocean will absorb more CFCs," Peidong Wang, a study lead co-author from MIT, explained in the press release. "When climate change warms the ocean, it becomes a weaker reservoir and will also outgas a little faster."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, the ocean's eventual release of CFC-11 is not dependent on the climate crisis. Instead, it is based on another mechanism, as &lt;a href="https://www.livescience.com/cfcs-release-from-oceans-ozone-destruction.html" target="_blank"&gt;LiveScience explained&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;[T]he ocean and atmosphere tend to stay in balance. When the atmosphere has a lot of a water-soluble molecule, like a CFC, the oceans suck some of it up. And when the oceans have a lot of that same molecule but the atmosphere doesn't, they tend to release it back into the air. As the world has stopped producing CFCs, atmospheric CFC levels have dropped, and the oceans are absorbing less and less from the air. Eventually, the balance will tip, and the oceans will become net-emitters of CFCs.&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;CFCs were commonly used in refrigerants, aerosols and household and industrial goods during the second half of the 20th century. They were thought to be non-toxic, non-flammable alternatives to substances such as ammonia and butane. However, they too broke down once released into the atmosphere, bonding with ozone and weakening the ozone layer that protects the planet from harmful ultraviolet radiation. This discovery led to CFCs being banned under the Montreal Protocol of 1987.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/cfc-ozone-ocean" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100772" data-published-at="1615912922" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;&lt;br&gt;However, during their heyday, oceans absorbed about five to ten percent of all CFC-11 emissions, the study authors wrote. When CFCs eventually release back into the atmosphere, their lifetime will be extended by five years. The researchers found that the ocean would continue to release CFC-11 until the end of their study period.&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"By the end of the run in 2300, the effect of the ocean on atmospheric CFC-11 remains significant," they wrote.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The scientists behind the study said that more work could be done to understand the interchange between the ocean, CFC-11 and the atmosphere.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Some of the next steps would be to do this with higher-resolution models and focus on patterns of change," Jeffery Scott, another MIT study co-author, said in the press release. "For now, we've opened up some great new questions and given an idea of what one might see."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>Every year, humpback whales migrate from polar regions to warmer waters, where they mate, give birth, raise their calves, and amaze whale watchers. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/humpback-whale-migration" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101213" data-published-at="1615909865" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;iframe style="border: none" src="//html5-player.libsyn.com/embed/episode/id/17955305/height/45/theme/standard/thumbnail/yes/direction/backward/" height="45" width="100%" scrolling="no"  allowfullscreen webkitallowfullscreen mozallowfullscreen oallowfullscreen msallowfullscreen&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;
</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/humpback-whale-migration" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101213" data-published-at="1615909865" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;"It's about just seeing a whale, seeing some of the acrobatic surface activity, from breaching and tail slapping  to bulls chasing females, even calves being born in the area," says Olaf Meynecke of Australia's Griffith University &lt;a target="_blank" href="https://whalesandclimate.org/"&gt;Whales and Climate Research Program&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;He says eastern Australia is a hotspot for seeing the majestic animals.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But as the climate warms, migration timing is changing. For example, in Queensland's Hervey Bay, humpbacks often arrive and leave earlier than in the past.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/humpback-whale-migration" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651101213" data-published-at="1615909865" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;At the end of the season, tour boats sometimes have trouble even finding a whale.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"On top of that, we also of course have higher uncertainty in terms of weather," Maynecke says. "We actually started to get a lot more rain in the dry season because the ocean is still so warm."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That can make for a wet, uncomfortable day at sea.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Meynecke says whale-watching businesses will need to find ways to adapt  for example, by shifting the season dates or offering flexible bookings  so they can keep satisfying their customers, even as the climate warms.&lt;/p&gt;</div>

</div><div class="widget__body clearfix sm-mt-1"><div class="photo-credit">
        Residents are rescued amid flood waters following Hurricane Katrina on Aug. 30, 2005 in New Orleans, Louisiana (not included in the study). <em>JAMES NIELSEN / AFP via Getty Images</em>

"\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>Homes in redlined neighborhoods are 25% more likely to be flooded, according to a <a href="https://www.redfin.com/news/redlining-flood-risk/?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-8xXxbkhVLaJ1PW0H0uJau0dFo5r_Hh1lQv4eXb-np4jobHogvVvCF-z-glAqsxYsQm0i6BdZWi1eMTB1-xwYknF2FQEQ&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank">report</a> from the real estate firm Redfin.</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
                    &lt;p&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
                    
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/redlined-homes-flood-risk-racism" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100448" data-published-at="1615908162" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/climate-change" target="_self"&gt;Climate change&lt;/a&gt;, caused by burning fossil fuels like gas, oil, and coal, is increasing U.S. &lt;a href="http://www.ecowatch.com/tag/flooding" target="_self"&gt;flooding&lt;/a&gt; risk, and the report is yet another example of the &lt;a href="https://nexusmedianews.com/top_story/extreme-heat-racism-covid-19-cause-compounding-harm/?swcfpc=1&amp;amp;utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;amp;utm_medium=email&amp;amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-8mmXyA1fGFRx7B7d0nE_VVBJBdzqG2NQhJNNPRYzdP3wQQYU4dezWsjd4HCwLVQB3LCD9V0F6DeghqxQBam6DK-YOLLg&amp;amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;compounding harms&lt;/a&gt; caused by racism and climate change. Overlaying current flood risk assessments with maps of which neighborhoods were excluded from public investment via New Deal-era programs because of their high Black and immigrant populations  the &lt;a href="https://nexusmedianews.com/top_story/racist-redlining-legacies-heat-american-neighborhoods/?swcfpc=1&amp;amp;utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;amp;utm_medium=email&amp;amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-9rfo7bB_RXO4yGAuQh_h6oTqk5flDNnzKO-aWHufYGfqJj9NtluarqGgC1dRb0Sh6THki2UfoLIDogOwEhT0qPhKugHg&amp;amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;racist practice known as redlining&lt;/a&gt; for the color in which those neighborhoods were delineated on federal maps  shows how the effects of those racist policies persist today. &lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/redlined-homes-flood-risk-racism" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100448" data-published-at="1615908162" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;"The discrimination that happened in the past may seem like it happened a long time ago, but it compounds," Redfin chief economist Daryl Fairweather told CNN. "It's not like the historical practices that were discriminatory diminished in effect. It seems like they actually increase in effect." The populations of redlined areas today are 58.1% Black, Indigenous, and people of color compared to 40.4% in places deemed desirable by lenders, the report found. The report comes as E&amp;amp;E reports FEMA is beginning to evaluate not just how disasters disproportionately burden low-income people and people of color, but how disaster response has exacerbated those inequities.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/redlined-homes-flood-risk-racism" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651100448" data-published-at="1615908162" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;As reported by &lt;a href="https://news.trust.org/item/20210315194806-w5m3a/?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;amp;utm_medium=email&amp;amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-9iwaZIwEeLPzYQLnWMuxfcmP-56FNNZv9Yq1eGY10YiL-oiQkEUp7Dc4kGqrGSi6NpogEdEjz_ao6YnucFzlMqieG-Eg&amp;amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;Reuters&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;The study's authors pointed to a number of examples where communities of color suffered the most from storms.&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;When Hurricane Katrina hit New Orleans in 2005, four of the seven zip codes with the costliest flood damage were at least 75% Black, it said.&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;And as sea levels rise and flooding becomes more common - with 2020 a record-breaking year for Atlantic hurricanes - there are concerns that financial institutions like banks and insurers will raise costs for the worst-affected households.&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;Jesse Keenan, associate professor of real estate at the Tulane School of Architecture, calls this "bluelining."&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;Much like redlining, he told the Thomson Reuters Foundation, institutions could begin drawing their own lines around neighborhoods at environmental risk, dictating the terms and availability of mortgages.&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;Therefore, he said, federal investment in infrastructure is urgently needed to help mitigate these risks.&lt;/blockquote&gt;</div>

                    &lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;For a deeper dive:&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Redlined flooding risk: &lt;a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/15/business/redlined-homes-climate-change-flooding/index.html?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-9ewTuIaY8ZtXvjd68qLJTtRipTXhUXcT7ek6-TMtyHyze9vmgSp_1qAImWtYg82vLZ_vUDgcfHOWgwBQiM5b7q67C-0g&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;CNN&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/graphics/2021-flood-risk-redlining/?sref=oUjKJw8m&amp;utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-_IbnWxs-LUxxD3ydgS_e8yKUnnmMCdBlLnVsqAIAaXgBhuUJI1HljqIdYVB29ZWSnUtnwz-C6nYtWhwK2WdUBfQydC3w&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;Bloomberg&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://news.trust.org/item/20210315194806-w5m3a/?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-9iwaZIwEeLPzYQLnWMuxfcmP-56FNNZv9Yq1eGY10YiL-oiQkEUp7Dc4kGqrGSi6NpogEdEjz_ao6YnucFzlMqieG-Eg&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;Thomson Reuters Foundation&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://www.nationalmortgagenews.com/news/climate-change-escalates-flood-risk-in-redlined-communities-by-25?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-9PaBMBThFupABuvDZoCyNt6Jf8b085zU4mZBG3-yCf132efluj4cNchCgYYrN8vTj0E4fWbMgtjEayBj3N-BBJseBPLg&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;National Mortgage News&lt;/a&gt;; FEMA: &lt;a href="https://www.eenews.net/climatewire/2021/03/15/stories/1063727429?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-_cFkrF2ff-oZzBp06bRUtm6fnUp7F4QpgB6LqzWCHyuowo_nFNLiuOk-Qc7HO23uNoYt6qE0jcQFj_zFIuvXapwfXKVA&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;E&amp;E&lt;/a&gt;; Climate Signals background: &lt;a href="https://www.climatesignals.org/climate-change-flooding?utm_campaign=Hot%20News&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;_hsmi=116139904&amp;_hsenc=p2ANqtz-_HvAt1trLkZMTxY02hp1bcJXdNP4_UzVzC58h1bhxNHAUcnmc74rFHfXQ81SfiCFw21ApBU3t6W_LTOL76u4Sz2OOQkg&amp;utm_content=116139904&amp;utm_source=hs_email" target="_blank"&gt;Flooding&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://newsletter.climatenexus.org/e2t/tc/VVVxRH94zHZ7W6_Zts46XCJC5W3GjFly4pd8mbN7qyl0y3p_9rV1-WJV7CgzPQW9cHhkS3t_5dxW8JCs2T8w6GltLsjbRLmbgwW14gH401p7tmrW35pWY_7r-gytW2YqWly8sr5sjW9lfxpT2GKNZNW8lTQ198LF8k0W8kzDW02DC70yW86p1Kb7KjGDfVZQWlg1MBb3TW23QC-J8120T8VhV56P6gHs6MW6sdvfS6lcs3kW2ZdgT88YdYXZW5HWNJW7cHlT2W45szmj74XZLdW6RPLRb4_fsgkW2HYxgY6dtK5HW782KWV31NMMsW5bw_gP6D7Fr2W6hc9-w4J6whKN7jR-_LXsjdPW4vPL7G2SfxHbW8jr-DR8n3Sp7W25wK1d8nmKrl3qdM1" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;em&gt;For more &lt;/em&gt;&lt;a href="http://ecowatch.com/climate-change-news/" target="_blank"&gt;&lt;em&gt;climate change&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;em&gt; </div><div class="widget__head"><a aria-label="Curiosity Is Killing Harpy Eagles in Central and South America" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/harpy-eagle-killings-2651100499.html">
